<dl><dt>Notes</dt></dl>
<ul><li><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_2"><b><a href="#ref_2">^2</a></b></span>  – Both <a href="/wiki/Olivier_Panis" title="Olivier Panis">Olivier Panis</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jos_Verstappen" title="Jos Verstappen">Jos Verstappen</a> received a 25-second post-race time penalty for overtaking under yellow flag conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-PanisVilleneuvePenalty_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PanisVilleneuvePenalty-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Death_of_Graham_Beveridge_and_inquiries">Death of Graham Beveridge and inquiries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2001_Australian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Death of Graham Beveridge and inquiries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The death of spectator marshal Graham Beveridge overshadowed the race. He was the first track marshal to die from injuries sustained during a Formula One race since <a href="/wiki/Paolo_Gislimberti" title="Paolo Gislimberti">Paolo Gislimberti</a> at the <a href="/wiki/2000_Italian_Grand_Prix" title="2000 Italian Grand Prix">2000 Italian Grand Prix</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-AtlasF1Race_2-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AtlasF1Race-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He predeceased his wife and three adult children.<sup id="cite_ref-BeveridgeTribute_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeveridgeTribute-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> At the request of his family, his death was not made public during the event,<sup id="cite_ref-BeveridgeTribute_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeveridgeTribute-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> and Michael Schumacher announced Beveridge had died, at the post-race press conference.<sup id="cite_ref-HSunAPSafer_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSunAPSafer-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> The day after the race, Beveridge's family spent more than half an hour visiting the accident site and the crash was explained by a race official.<sup id="cite_ref-BeveridgeTribute_75-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BeveridgeTribute-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> CAMS and <a href="/wiki/National_Australia_Bank" title="National Australia Bank">National Australia Bank</a> formed a trust fund for his family for individuals to donate to,<sup id="cite_ref-:1_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> and a subsequent public auction to sell Formula One memorabilia raised more than A$100,000.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> On 9 March, a memorial service was held at the St. Jude's Anglican Church in Beveridge's hometown of <a href="/wiki/Bowral" title="Bowral">Bowral</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_South_Wales" title="New South Wales">New South Wales</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> He was buried at the Bundaberg General Cemetery four days later.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> A park bench opposite turn three was dedicated in his memory at a commemoration service on 9 November 2002.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The race stewards investigated the crash and chose not to pursue any action against Villeneuve and Ralf Schumacher. They rated the crash "a racing incident", with neither driver to blame. The FIA launched an inquiry as Villeneuve's car was impounded on the order of the <a href="/wiki/Coroners_Court_of_Victoria" title="Coroners Court of Victoria">state coroner of Victoria</a> <a href="/wiki/Graeme_Johnstone" title="Graeme Johnstone">Graeme Johnstone</a> for his investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> The section of catchfence that Villeneuve's right-rear wheel penetrated was stored at the Victoria Police's traffic centre in Brunswick.<sup id="cite_ref-DriveInquiry_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DriveInquiry-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Both Villeneuve and Ralf Schumacher were interviewed by officers from the <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Police" title="Victoria Police">Victoria Police</a>'s Major Collision Investigation Unit.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup> The FIA's investigation was completed on 3 August. In its confidential report, the organisers of the race, the Australian Grand Prix Corporation (AGPC), were absolved of any responsibility for the death of Beveridge, which it called "a freak accident", and discovered the marshal was stationed at an incorrect position at the time of the crash.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Coronial_inquest">Coronial inquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2001_Australian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Coronial inquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Following the Victoria Police Major Collision Investigation Unit examination lasting eight months and also absolved the AGPC, on 3 December 2001 the official inquest into the death of Beveridge opened in Melbourne.<sup id="cite_ref-DriveInquiry_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DriveInquiry-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> The FIA severed all formal links with the inquest and withdrew instructions to local lawyers to act on its behalf. The governing body's own appointee, the race director and permanent starter <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Whiting" title="Charlie Whiting">Charlie Whiting</a>, did not appear in person or provide evidence by satellite.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>During the inquest, the court was told Beveridge was instructed to stand at the fence opening to prevent spectators from accessing the track and it had prevented any further fatalities.<sup id="cite_ref-TCM4Dec01_55-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-TCM4Dec01-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> The issue over the height of the catchfence was then raised by the inquest. <a href="/wiki/Tim_Schenken" title="Tim Schenken">Tim Schenken</a>, a member of CAMS, said some of the fences were raised in height by 1&#160;m (39&#160;in) before the <a href="/wiki/1999_Australian_Grand_Prix" title="1999 Australian Grand Prix">1999 race</a> albeit he had no knowledge if a formal risk analysis report was carried out to assess the potential danger to marshals and spectators.<sup id="cite_ref-MarshalFlew_58-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarshalFlew-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup> Following this, a safety engineer was called to the stand. He said the fence was too low and a Formula One car could cartwheel over it if a collision occurred. He also theorised debris could be projected for around 300&#160;m (980&#160;ft) past the fence and be launched as high as 22&#160;m (72&#160;ft) into the air.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> A British track marshal told the court this had twice been the case at the <a href="/wiki/Silverstone_Circuit" title="Silverstone Circuit">Silverstone Circuit</a> in the United Kingdom. The inquest later heard the AGPC rejected Whiting's suggestion to increase the height of the fences in 1998 and 2001, something CAMS and the AGPC denied.<sup id="cite_ref-HSunAPSafer_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HSunAPSafer-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The court was then shown a video of <a href="/wiki/Martin_Brundle" title="Martin Brundle">Martin Brundle</a>'s airborne accident on the first lap of the 1996 race which occurred at the same corner Beveridge died at. The manager of safety services for CAMS stated he could not recall any meeting to discuss the crash and no investigation occurred since nobody was injured. Villeneuve's damaged car was brought into the court to explain why its wheel tethers failed in the accident. It was told while the car met FIA international standards dictating the wheel tethers to withstand 500&#160;t (490 long tons; 550 short tons) of pressure, three of them failed in the collision. The BAR technical director <a href="/wiki/Malcolm_Oastler" title="Malcolm Oastler">Malcolm Oastler</a> said the design of the wheel tether was changed following the accident.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On 19 December, the final submissions were made to the inquest. <a href="/wiki/Jim_Kennan" title="Jim Kennan">Jim Kennan</a>, the counsel assisting the coroner, argued the organisation that should be held responsible for Beveridge's death was the AGPC under the Australian Grand Prix Act, "No one organisation accepted ultimate responsibility for the design – AGPC relied on CAMS, CAMS relied on FIA, the FIA said the local promoter had ultimate responsibility."<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> Johnstone's report was released on 8 February 2002. It agreed with Kennan's suggestion the AGPC was the sole company responsible for Beveridge's death due to it not analysing the risks to marshals and concluded the accident was "avoidable".<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Physician.27s_inquest"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Physician's_inquest">Physician's inquest</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=2001_Australian_Grand_Prix&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Physician&#039;s inquest">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In December 2002, the <a href="/wiki/Medical_Practitioners_Board_of_Victoria" title="Medical Practitioners Board of Victoria">Medical Practitioners Board of Victoria</a> opened an investigation into the professional conduct of three senior physicians who treated Beveridge at the scene of the accident when Johnstone's report revealed medical records had been altered to disguise the fact the marshal died at the track.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> It found a physician was told via telephone resuscitation on Beveridge had stopped at 14:47 local time and he subsequently ordered the nurse who produced the record to delete it.<sup id="cite_ref-PMNov03_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMNov03-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> One physician said he had an obligation to transport casualties and fatalities to The Alfred Hospital for their official certification of death.<sup id="cite_ref-SMHJul03_60-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SMHJul03-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Two of three senior physicians were found guilty of professional misconduct by the four-member panel on 7 November 2003.<sup id="cite_ref-PMNov03_57-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PMNov03-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> In June 2004, an appeals tribunal reversed the unprofessional conduct decision on the chief medical officer, who deemed he had committed an "error of judgement".<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
